The Story of World Literature (186)

— Written by John Macy of the United States, translated by Hu Zhongchi

Chapter 48: Essays and History of Literary America

America's specialized historians have achieved excellent work. I am referring to those historians who are doing excellent work in the history of recording. Washington Irving's research on American and Spanish history is superior to creating the mild and humorous figure of Rip and Nickbacker's father. He paid homage to the young Prescott, who had begun to study and write the history of Mexico, with great courtesy, because he was blind and hindered. The history of Mexico made Prescott famous, and he went on to engage in the study of "The Conquest of Peru," followed by the history of "Philip II." I know from later historians that much of his work has been abandoned as history. However, he did not make any mistakes in the facts as far as the facts could be obtained. His books are still readable today. I am not giving testimony to historians, but to literary figures.

Mark Twain said when making essays and history of the books he treasured, "Parkman's thousand volumes if he wrote that much." Parkman had a greater interest in the northwest of America and the struggle between the English and French before the founding of the American Republic than "La Salle" and "Montcalm and Wolfe." Strict scientific historians may have attacked Parkman as a romantic. However, the subject matter he dealt with for years was essentially romantic, and although his book was not accurate until the last narrative, it was always persuasive until the last article.

Chapter 49: American Poetry

I hear the song of America, a changing chorus, I hear

— Whitman

Among all the forms of literature, among the specimens of all the forms written on the northwest coast of the Atlantic, American poetry has the least of the content and color and the unique vitality of the continent where the poetry is written. Apart from Whitman, who many readers do not regard as a representative of the American spirit, and apart from two or three poems written in local or ethnic dialects that describe several poems of scenery and subject matter that are especially peculiar to this country, most of American poetry can be said to have been written by English minor poets.

The derivative, subordinate, and secondary nature of American poetry is not necessarily evidence of the subservience of American poets, but is one of the things that proves the overwhelming power of English poetry. We can think in American style in prose, but we must sing in English style. American poets often do not feel like the French, Germans, and English do about their own country or a part of the country they live in. The issue of patriotism is not at all present here. The muse despises patriots unless she can make music from patriotism, and a poet's being an American is ultimately less important than a poet's being a poet.

Page 19

Book and Newspaper Introduction

Inaugural Issue of "Era Youth"

— Guangmei

Sold on behalf of Da Guang Bookstore

The moment the words "youth" are mentioned, one immediately imagines lively, strong, and energetic young men. Youth is the most precious stage of life. The expectations for youth are exceptionally profound. Everyone knows that youth is the vitality of the nation and the hope for the life of the country and its people. The rise and fall of a nation depends on the state of its youth. The responsibility borne by youth is indeed significant. However, during their schooling, many outstanding students are unwilling to devote their aspirations to mastering what they learn, aiming to reach the pinnacle and serve society and the nation. But the reality is not so simple. After graduation, they often fail to achieve their goals. If we simply observe China in the past and even now, how many people with specialized knowledge, especially in agriculture, industry, and commerce, have their wishes fulfilled and are employed by the government? The idea of the government providing financial support for someone to study a certain science for life is even more of a fantasy. Even those who are employed by the government are often not using what they studied. Once these "learned-but-not-used" gentlemen take up important positions, their personal concerns are no longer an issue. They may still have the initial intention and plan to revitalize the country, but only on the political stage do they realize that many things cannot be carried out according to their ideals. Unable to fulfill their initial aspirations, it goes without saying that they become assimilated over time, becoming no different from the old guard. Under these circumstances, youth then generate the following two thoughts: firstly, the government does not pay enough attention to specialized talents and is therefore unwilling to focus on research; secondly, young students also compromise. As a result, the future prospects of youth become a major problem. Disappointment in their prospects inevitably leads to discouragement. In this way, all kinds of "isms"—defeatism, romanticism, decadence, pessimism, corruption, and deterioration—emerge endlessly. With the state of youth being such, coupled with the inherent static, conservative national character, we, the youth, naturally form this weak and unhealthy phenomenon, which has a great impact on the future of the nation. This phenomenon cannot be ignored today.

I have often said that from secondary schools upwards, no matter what school, if you analyze the personality, thoughts, and behavior of the hundreds or thousands of students within, you will find everything imaginable. The reason for this is the lack of a unified central ideology. Not only is this the case for the students themselves, but it is also related to the books they read. Chinese books lack a consistent central ideology, and China is a country that lags behind in everything. Therefore, much knowledge must be borrowed from foreign countries. Those gentlemen who are obsessed with foreign goods consider even the dregs of foreign goods to be precious. Furthermore, teachers also lack a consistent central consciousness regarding the future of the Chinese nation. They simply go their own way, even introducing ideologies and theories that harm the nation. This erroneous view creates the current state of ideological confusion in the entire youth sector.

We dare to believe that because youth lack a unified central ideology, they are dissatisfied with reality. Some are dissatisfied with reality but do not know how to reform it; others want to transform it but have no way to do so. Naturally, they feel pain in their minds. However, dissatisfaction with reality is not a bad phenomenon; otherwise, society would not evolve. In the future, the issue of guiding youth's thinking should be to bring youth with various different thoughts and paths onto the right track and establish a central ideology. History tells us that the only way to save the Chinese nation from danger is to awaken national consciousness as the center. However, there are very few publications of this kind. Since reading the "Manifesto of the Nationalist Literary Movement" published by the Chinese Nationalist Literary Movement on June 1st, followed by the publication of "Avant-Garde Weekly," this is certainly a cause for rejoicing. Recently, I discovered another youth publication, "Era Youth," and must once again solemnly introduce it to our young comrades.

Last night, I went to Da Guang Bookstore in Ximen to buy books. Upon entering, the first thing that caught my eye was not the artistic novel covers, but the newspaper-like "Era Youth." This is the inaugural issue of the publication. In addition to the inaugural editorial, there are Tang Zenghongyang's "Anatomy of the Morbid State of Modern Chinese Youth," Tie Seng's "A Bird's-Eye View of the Anti-Imperialist Movement of the World's Weak and Small Nations and the Way Out for the Chinese Nation to Seek Freedom and Equality," Xia Xuan's "Written Before the Era Youth," Zhu Jianbai's "Our Future Understanding of Literature and Art," Xu Zexiang's "Marching Forward for the Nation," and Yi De's "Era Youth."

I cannot copy the content of each article in detail. Let the readers enjoy them themselves. We only need to look at Li Zhengjun's words in the inaugural editorial to understand the attitude and purpose of the publication: "...The current chaotic state of the entire youth sector, how can we establish a central ideology? This is the primary requirement of this publication. What we ask is that the youth of the whole country work together to build a lighthouse in this stormy sea to guide youth. Secondly, we feel that the dispersal of the power of the youth sector is always a crisis for the country and the nation. This small publication focuses on gathering the scattered youth through resonance and consensus... Furthermore, we observe that in addition to the chaotic and negative phenomena in the youth sector, we also see a worse kind of decline... Perhaps there will be sincere comfort for the decadent youth. In addition, there are theoretical aspects of the youth movement that we want to contribute to this publication, but this is a major issue. We hope that the youth of the whole country will have a heated discussion on this. In addition, research on politics and economics and discussions on social issues are necessary methods for youth to seek knowledge, which is another mission..." From the above meaning, we can know the contribution of this publication to the youth sector. Therefore, I solemnly introduce it, hoping that our young people will have a copy in hand.

Franklin's Writings

Franklin's writings were recently compiled by Henry Srmytbe Jr., entitled "The Amazing Benjamin Franklin," and will be published by the Pennsylvania Branch of the Society of the Descendants of the American Revolution, printed by Franklin Printing Company, which Franklin founded in 1728. The book contains praise from contemporary celebrities, the most well-known of whom include US Treasury Secretary Mellon, Labor Secretary Davis, British Ambassador to the US Howard, and former French President Millerand.

Chaucer's Writings

Chaucer is the father of English literature. His "Canterbury Tales" is an immortal work. In the recent months, three editions are to be printed. One is included in the Modern Library series, one is a combined edition of the original text (Old English) and modern translation with twenty-four full-page illustrations, and another is published exclusively in modern English. The publication period is probably in April, which is most appropriate according to his prologue.

Wells' "Outline of World History"

Wells' "Outline of World History" was originally quite expensive. Recently, the American Garden City Publishing Company has included it in the One Dollar Collection. The plates used are no different from the Five Dollar version.

Complete Collection of Shakespeare's Poems

The American Morrow Company recently hired Yale University professor Brooke to compile Shakespeare's Complete Collection of Poems. The motivation was that a lady wanted to search for a complete collection in London last year but could not find one. It is said that the first edition has luxurious binding and is limited to only five hundred copies, which has already been completely sold out. The second edition has a smaller format and an unlimited number of copies.

Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introduction Manuscripts

(1) The text is limited to the introduction of the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all books and newspapers on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc. are included in the introduction, but vulgar books will not be introduced.

Drawings are limited to the latest works of new writers at home and abroad and related illustrations to the text.

(2) Articles on textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(3) Pictures and photos are limited to those related to the text.

(4) Each text should not exceed three thousand words at most.
